## Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures

Kenneth L. Clarkson
IBM Research
вҖғвҖғ
Shashanka Ubaru
IBM Research
вҖғвҖғ
Elizabeth Yang
University of California, Berkeley; part of this work was done at IBM Research

##### Abstract

Hyperdimensional computing (HDC) is a biologically-inspired framework which represents symbols with high-dimensional vectors, and uses vector operations to manipulate them.
The ensemble of a particular vector space and a prescribed set of vector operations (including one addition-like for вҖңbundlingвҖқ and one outer-product-like for вҖңbindingвҖқ) form a *vector symbolic architecture* (VSA).
While VSAs have been employed in numerous applications and have been studied empirically, many theoretical questions about VSAs remain open.

We analyze the *representation capacities* of four common VSAs: MAP-I, MAP-B, and two VSAs based on sparse binary vectors.
вҖңRepresentation capacityвҖқ here refers to bounds on the dimensions of the VSA vectors required to perform certain symbolic tasks, such as testing for set membership iвҲҲSрқ‘–рқ‘Ҷi\in S and estimating set intersection sizes |XвҲ©Y|рқ‘Ӣрқ‘Ң|X\cap Y| for two sets of symbols Xрқ‘ӢX and Yрқ‘ҢY, to a given degree of accuracy.
We also analyze the ability of a novel variant of a Hopfield network (a simple model of associative memory) to perform some of the same tasks that are typically asked of VSAs.

In addition to providing new bounds on VSA capacities, our analyses establish and leverage connections between VSAs, вҖңsketchingвҖқ (dimensionality reduction) algorithms, and Bloom filters.

### 1 Introduction

*Hyperdimensional computing* (HDC) is a biologically inspired framework for representing symbolic information.
In this framework, we represent different symbols using high-dimensional vectors (hypervectors), called *atomic vectors*, sampled from a natural vector distribution, such as random signed vectors, or sparse binary vectors.
We then use standard arithmetic or bit-wise operations on these vectors to perform symbolic operations, like associating or grouping symbols.
The distribution over atomic vectors, together with their corresponding operations, form a *vector-symbolic architecture* (VSA).

Many features of VSAs are inspired by aspects of the human brain and memory.
They are robust to noise, and the fact that all entries of the vectors are symmetric (i.e. donвҖҷt correspond to specific features) allows VSA computations to be highly parallelizable.
Most VSA vector entries are either 00 or Вұ1plus-or-minus1\pm 1, so there is no need for floating point arithmetic, and they admit energy-efficient and low-latency hardware implementations.

In VSA systems, the atomic vectors are typically chosen randomly, with a distribution such that they are highly likely to be pairwise *near-orthogonal*.

While we encounter вҖңthe curse of dimensionalityвҖқ in many algorithmic and machine learning problems, the ability to fit many near-orthogonal vectors into dрқ‘‘d-dimensional space is a kind of вҖңblessing of dimensionality.вҖқ

While VSAs sometimes do not achieve the same performance as neural networks do on certain classification tasks, VSA-based classifiers require much less time and space to train and store.
There is also much research at the intersection of VSAs and deep learning; for instance, VSA vector representations could be good neural network inputs, and since all vector representations have the same size, this could be a better way to support inputs with different numbers of features ([kleyko2019distributed, alonso2021hyperembed]).
In addition, VSAs have found numerous applications outside of learning, including the modeling of sensory-motor systems in smaller organisms ([kleyko2015fly, kleyko2015imitation]), combining word embeddings to form context embeddings ([kanerva2000random, sahlgren2005introduction, jones2007representing]), and the processing of heart rate respiratory data and other biological times series data ([kleyko2018vector, kleyko2019hyperdimensional, burrello2019hyperdimensional]).
They are also promising tools for bridging the gap between symbolic data, such as word relationships, and numerical data, such as trained word embeddings ([quiroz2020semantic]).

In addition to exploring the performance of VSAs in such applications, there have also been several works that study the *representation capacity* of many VSAs.
The representation capacity refers to lower bounds on the VSA dimension, needed so that we can reliably perform certain symbolic tasks, such as computing set intersection sizes |XвҲ©Y|рқ‘Ӣрқ‘Ң|X\cap Y| for two sets of symbols Xрқ‘ӢX and Yрқ‘ҢY (with possibly different cardinalities).
These lower bounds then translate into a design choice (minimum required dimension) for VSA applications.
Here we understand reliability in the setting of generating the atomic vectors at random, and asking for good-enough accuracy with high-enough probability.
Similarly, another way to quantify representation capacity is the following: if we tolerate a failure probability of Оҙрқӣҝ\delta, can we bound the number of sets or objects we can encode?

The goal of this paper is to provide theoretical analyses of the representation capacities of four particular VSA models.
In general, there are far more models that are employed in practice; see [schlegel2022comparison, kleyko\_survey\_2021-1] for a longer catalog of VSAs.
We also assemble a set of tools and frameworks (common to computer scientists) for any future computations and high-probability bounds on VSA capacity.

#### 1.1 Background on VSAs

To define a VSA, we need to first choose a distribution for sampling the atomic vectors.
For every individual symbol we want to introduce (that is, excluding associations between multiple symbols), we will independently sample a random mрқ‘ҡm-dimensional vector from a distribution, such as the uniform one over {Вұ1}msuperscriptplus-or-minus1рқ‘ҡ\{\pm 1\}^{m} (i.e. sign vectors), or a random kрқ‘ҳk-sparse binary ({0,1}msuperscript01рқ‘ҡ\{0,1\}^{m}) vector.
VSAs are equipped with the following operations; permutation is not always required.

* вҖў

  Similarity Measurement (вҹЁвӢ…,вӢ…вҹ©
  вӢ…вӢ…\langle\cdot,\cdot\rangle):
  In almost all VSAs in this paper, we use cosine similarity (i.e. dot product вҹЁu,vвҹ©
  рқ‘ўрқ‘Ј\langle u,v\rangle) to measure the similarity between the symbols that uрқ‘ўu and vрқ‘Јv represent.
* вҖў

  Bundling (вҠ•direct-sum\oplus): We use bundling to represent a вҖңunionвҖқ of several symbols. The goal is for uвҠ•vdirect-sumрқ‘ўрқ‘Јu\oplus v to be similar to both uрқ‘ўu and vрқ‘Јv.
* вҖў

  Binding (вҠ—tensor-product\otimes): Binding is often used to associate symbols as (key, value) pairs.
  Here, we want uвҠ—vtensor-productрқ‘ўрқ‘Јu\otimes v to be nearly orthogonal to both uрқ‘ўu and vрқ‘Јv.
* вҖў

  Permutation (ПҖрқңӢ\pi): If ПҖрқңӢ\pi is a permutation, let ПҖвҖӢ(v)рқңӢрқ‘Ј\pi(v) be the vector whose iрқ‘–i-th entry is vПҖвҲ’1вҖӢ(i)subscriptрқ‘ЈsuperscriptрқңӢ1рқ‘–v\_{\pi^{-1}(i)}.
  We use [v1;ПҖвҖӢ(v2);ПҖ2вҖӢ(v3);вҖҰ;ПҖLвҲ’1вҖӢ(vL)]
  subscriptрқ‘Ј1рқңӢsubscriptрқ‘Ј2superscriptрқңӢ2subscriptрқ‘Ј3вҖҰsuperscriptрқңӢрқҗҝ1subscriptрқ‘Јрқҗҝ[v\_{1};\;\pi(v\_{2});\;\pi^{2}(v\_{3});\;\ldots;\pi^{L-1}(v\_{L})] to encode an *ordered sequence* of symbols or sets.
* вҖў

  Cleanup: Let vector xрқ‘Ҙx represent a set XвҠҶрқ’ірқ‘Ӣрқ’іX\subseteq\mathcal{X}, where рқ’ірқ’і\mathcal{X} is the universe of all symbols.
  Given a dictionary of symbols SвҠҶрқ’ірқ‘Ҷрқ’іS\subseteq\mathcal{X}, we want to compute the elements in XвҲ©Sрқ‘Ӣрқ‘ҶX\cap S.

##### Remark 1.

  Cleanup will not be a focus of our paper.
  If we have access to the individual vector representations of elements in Sрқ‘ҶS, we can simply execute cleanup as a set of (parallel) membership tests, which use similarity measurement.

##### Example 1.

We can represent categorical data using the following bundle of bindings:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | yвҶ’=вЁҒiвҲҲВ featuresfвҶ’iвҠ—vвҶ’iвҶ’рқ‘Ұsubscriptdirect-sumрқ‘–В featurestensor-productsubscriptвҶ’рқ‘“рқ‘–subscriptвҶ’рқ‘Јрқ‘–\vec{y}=\bigoplus\_{i\in\text{ features}}\vec{f}\_{i}\otimes\vec{v}\_{i} |  |

Here, fвҶ’isubscriptвҶ’рқ‘“рқ‘–\vec{f}\_{i} is a VSA vector encoding the concept вҖңfeature iрқ‘–i,вҖқ while vвҶ’isubscriptвҶ’рқ‘Јрқ‘–\vec{v}\_{i} is a VSA vector encoding the value of feature iрқ‘–i.
To train a classifier on the VSA representations {yвҶ’}вҶ’рқ‘Ұ\{\vec{y}\}, we can average the training vectors over each class to get an exemplar for the class.

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | cвҶ’i=1#вҖӢ{z:В labelвҖӢ(z)=i}вҖӢвҲ‘z:В labelвҖӢ(z)=izsubscriptвҶ’рқ‘җрқ‘–1#conditional-setрқ‘§В labelрқ‘§рқ‘–subscript:рқ‘§В labelрқ‘§рқ‘–рқ‘§\vec{c}\_{i}=\frac{1}{\#\{z:\text{ label}(z)=i\}}\sum\_{z:\text{ label}(z)=i}z |  |

To classify a new input, we first compute its VSA encoding.
We then return the class whose representative vector cisubscriptрқ‘җрқ‘–c\_{i} is closest to it (using similarity measurement).

We will study a few basic predicates on VSAs; one is *membership testing*: given a vector xрқ‘Ҙx representing a bundle of atomic vectors, and an atomic vector yрқ‘Ұy, determine if yрқ‘Ұy is in the set represented by xрқ‘Ҙx.
Another predicate is *set intersection*: if yрқ‘Ұy also represents a set, estimate the size of the intersection of the sets represented by xрқ‘Ҙx and yрқ‘Ұy.
Here these sets might be sets of vectors bound together, or permuted.
Estimation of intersection size is a natural extension of membership testing, and is helpful in applications where VSA represent, for example, sets of properties, where intersection and difference size are rough measure of relatedness.

#### 1.2 Overview of Contributions and Related Work

We focus on four popular VSA families, plus a novel variant of Hopfield networks.
The atomic vector initializations of the four, as well as their bundling and binding operators, are shown in TableВ [1](#S1.T1 "Table 1 вҖЈ 1.2 Overview of Contributions and Related Work вҖЈ 1 Introduction вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures").
As surveyed by [schlegel2022comparison], вҖңMAPвҖқ stands for вҖңMultiply-Add-Permute,вҖқ while вҖңIвҖқ and вҖңBвҖқ reference the values that non-atomic vectors take (вҖңintegerвҖқ and вҖңbinary,вҖқ respectively).

| VSA | Atomic Vector | Bundling | Binding |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| MAP-I | {Вұ1}msuperscriptplus-or-minus1рқ‘ҡ\{\pm 1\}^{m} | Elem.-wise addition | Elem.-wise mult. |
| MAP-B | {Вұ1}msuperscriptplus-or-minus1рқ‘ҡ\{\pm 1\}^{m} | Elem.-wise add., round to Вұ1plus-or-minus1\pm 1 | Elem.-wise mult |
| Bloom filters | kрқ‘ҳk-sparse, {0,1}msuperscript01рқ‘ҡ\{0,1\}^{m} | Elem.-wise addition, cap at 1 | (Out of scope) |
| Counting Bloom filters | kрқ‘ҳk-sparse, {0,1}msuperscript01рқ‘ҡ\{0,1\}^{m} | Elem.-wise addition | (Out of scope) |

Table 1: 
A summary of MAP-I, MAP-B, and Binary Sparse VSAs (which generalize SBDR VSAs). While several binding operators have been proposed for the Binary Sparse VSAs, the study of these operators is outside of the scope of this paper.

A key aspect of our analyses is that we translate several VSA operations of interest into the language of sketching matrices (used for dimensionality reduction) or of hashing-based data structures (like Bloom Filters), which are all well-studied objects in computer science.
These connections have not been made explicit, or leveraged previously in VSA analysis, though we remark that Sparse-JL was briefly mentioned by [thomas\_streaming\_2022].

##### 1.2.1 Connections to the Broader Computer Science Literature

In several of our analyses, we rely on the Johnson-Lindenstrauss (JL) property, which is foundational to algorithmic matrix sketching, the study of techniques for compressing matrices while approximately preserving key properties, such as least-squares solutions.
See [woodruff\_computational\_2014] for a more detailed treatment of sketching.
From the perspective of sketching, our results on permutations, bundles of kрқ‘ҳk-bindings, and Hopfield networks can be regarded as extensions of sketching theory using structured matrices with less randomness than the most direct approaches.

The bundling operator for MAP-B is per-coordinate the *Majority function* in the setting of the analysis of Boolean functions, and is a simple *linear threshold function*. The analysis of the membership test for MAP-B that we give is close to that for analyzing the *influence* of variables for the majority function (cf. [o2014analysis], Exer. 2.2).
Here the influence of a variable on a function is the probability for a random input that the function return value changes when the variable is negated. In comparison, in the analysis of MAP-B bundling, we are interested in the probability that the return value changes when the variable is set to +11+1.
Our analysis of MAP-B extends to other operations, including a bundling of bindings, which are related to *polynomial threshold functions* of degreeВ kрқ‘ҳk, where kрқ‘ҳk depends on the maximum number of symbols that are bound together.

Two of the VSAs we analyze are based on Bloom filters, which are space-efficient data structures for testing set membership.
They have seen extensive study since their introduction fifty years ago by [bloom\_spacetime\_1970], but we have not found rigorous analyses of their performance in the setting of set intersection (vs membership testing).
Our results are novel contributions in this regard.

##### 1.2.2 Other Analyses of VSA Capacity

Some recent works in the VSA literature that have inspired our own work also study the capacity problem, but they analyze more restricted VSA systems and/or use different analysis approaches.
To our knowledge, we are the first to formally analyze VSAs in terms of sketching, using tools like the JL property, though [thomas\_streaming\_2022] does mention the sparse JL transform.

[thomas\_theoretical\_2021] provides a theoretical analysis of VSAs in terms of a measure called вҖңincoherence,вҖқ which quantifies the size of the вҖңcross-talkвҖқ (dot product) between two independently initialized VSA vectors.
They prove results on membership testing and set intersection of bundles, membership testing in key-value pairs (bindings of two symbols, keys and values, where the set of keys and the set of values are restricted to be disjoint), and show pairwise near-orthogonality of vectors and their coordinate permutations in terms of incoherence. Their work is in the linear setting (which pertains to MAP-I), and extends, as does ours via known results, from sign matrices to matrices of independent sub-Gaussians.
We add new bounds that include set intersections for bundles of kрқ‘ҳk-bindings (not restricted to disjoint keys and values), and sequences of sets encoded with rotations (cyclic permutations).
Our view of sketching is potentially simpler for understanding capacity bounds on MAP-I, and our hypergraph framework for binding in В§[4.3](#S4.SS3 "4.3 Binding вҖЈ 4 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") also allows us to extend our analysis for bundlings of bindings beyond only key-value pairs.

Another related work is that of [kleyko\_classification\_2018], which studies bundling in binary VSA systems, where atomic vectors are controlled by a sparsity parameter.
Their model is slightly different from the Bloom-filter inspired binary VSAs that we analyze, and their bundling operator includes a вҖңthinningвҖқ step, where the support of the bundle gets reduced to the size of a typical atomic vector.
Their analysis of VSA capacity uses Gaussian approximations holding in the limit, and some heuristics to get around the thinning step.
We formally analyze the capacity of bundling without thinning, using concentration inequalities.
The authors in [kleyko\_classification\_2018] also conduct several empirical analyses and simulations of sparse binary VSAs, which may be of independent interest.

### 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results

In the remainder of the paper, we will present concrete statements of our results, and highlight some of the proof ideas, with an emphasis again on connections to sketching and data structures.
Each subsection here (roughly organized by each different VSA we analyze) will have a full section in the appendix where we give their proofs.

#### 2.1 Bundling as the output of a linear map.

Our central approach is to cast VSA vectors as the outputs of linear transformations, followed by nonlinear maps for some of the VSAs.
Via the linear maps, we can translate between a very simple vector representation for symbols (described below) and the more robust, fault-tolerant, and (in some settings) lower-dimensional ones used in VSAs.

A simple vector representation of elements in a universe рқ’ірқ’і\mathcal{X} is their one-hot encoding as unit binary vectors eiвҲҲ{0,1}dsubscriptрқ‘’рқ‘–superscript01рқ‘‘e\_{i}\in\{0,1\}^{d}, where dвүЎ|рқ’і|рқ‘‘рқ’іd\equiv|\mathcal{X}|.
Then, set union corresponds to adding vectors: a set XвҠӮрқ’ірқ‘Ӣрқ’іX\subset\mathcal{X} is a characteristic vector vвҲҲ{0,1}dрқ‘Јsuperscript01рқ‘‘v\in\{0,1\}^{d} with v=вҲ‘iвҲҲXeiрқ‘Јsubscriptрқ‘–рқ‘Ӣsubscriptрқ‘’рқ‘–v=\sum\_{i\in X}e\_{i}.
The size of |X|рқ‘Ӣ|X| corresponds to the squared Euclidean norm вҖ–vвҖ–2superscriptnormрқ‘Ј2\|v\|^{2}.
For two sets X,YвҠҶрқ’і

рқ‘Ӣрқ‘Ң
рқ’іX,Y\subseteq\mathcal{X} with corresponding characteristic vectors vрқ‘Јv and wрқ‘Өw, respectively, |XвҲ©Y|рқ‘Ӣрқ‘Ң|X\cap Y| is simply vвҠӨвҖӢwsuperscriptрқ‘Јtopрқ‘Өv^{\top}w; similarly, their symmetric difference |XвҖӢО”вҖӢY|рқ‘ӢО”рқ‘Ң|X\Delta Y| is вҖ–vвҲ’wвҖ–2superscriptnormрқ‘Јрқ‘Ө2\|v-w\|^{2}.

Thus an embedding of these one-hot encodings, linear or non-linear, that approximately preserves distances and/or dot products of vectors (which is particularly challenging for binary vectors), can be used to maintain sets and the sizes of their intersections and symmetric differences.
With this in mind, we can regard the atomic vectors of a VSA as the columns of a random matrix Pрқ‘ғP (so the embedding of vector xрқ‘Ҙx is PвҖӢxрқ‘ғрқ‘ҘPx, possibly with a non-linearity applied), and for appropriate random Pрқ‘ғP, we will obtain such embeddings.

A correspondence between the VSAs we study and their choice of matrix Pрқ‘ғP is found in TableВ [2](#S2.T2 "Table 2 вҖЈ 2.1 Bundling as the output of a linear map. вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures").
From this perspective, VSAs perform dimensionality reduction from characteristic vectors in {0,1}dsuperscript01рқ‘‘\{0,1\}^{d}
to an mрқ‘ҡm-dimensional space, for mвүӘdmuch-less-thanрқ‘ҡрқ‘‘m\ll d.

| VSA | Atomic Vector | Bundling |
| --- | --- | --- |
| MAP-I | SВҜвҖӢeiВҜрқ‘Ҷsubscriptрқ‘’рқ‘–{\bar{S}}e\_{i} | SВҜвҖӢvВҜрқ‘Ҷрқ‘Ј{\bar{S}}v |
| MAP-B | SвҖӢeiрқ‘Ҷsubscriptрқ‘’рқ‘–Se\_{i} | signвҒЎ(SвҖӢv)signрқ‘Ҷрқ‘Ј\operatorname{{\text{sign}}}(Sv) |
| Bloom filter | BвҖӢeiрқҗөsubscriptрқ‘’рқ‘–Be\_{i} | 1вҲ§BвҖӢv1рқҗөрқ‘Ј1\wedge Bv |
| Counting Bloom | BвҖӢeiрқҗөsubscriptрқ‘’рқ‘–Be\_{i} | BвҖӢvрқҗөрқ‘ЈBv |

Table 2: 
Equivalent to TableВ [1](#S1.T1 "Table 1 вҖЈ 1.2 Overview of Contributions and Related Work вҖЈ 1 Introduction вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"). Here eiвҲҲ{0,1}dsubscriptрқ‘’рқ‘–superscript01рқ‘‘e\_{i}\in\{0,1\}^{d} for iвҲҲ[d]рқ‘–delimited-[]рқ‘‘i\in[d] has ei=1subscriptрқ‘’рқ‘–1e\_{i}=1, all other coordinates zero, and vвҲҲ{0,1}dрқ‘Јsuperscript01рқ‘‘v\in\{0,1\}^{d} represents the set suppвҒЎ(v)вҠӮ[d]suppрқ‘Јdelimited-[]рқ‘‘\operatorname{{\text{supp}}}(v)\subset[d]. The matrices Sрқ‘ҶS, SВҜВҜрқ‘Ҷ{\bar{S}}, and BрқҗөB are sign (also called bipolar or Rademacher), scaled sign, and sparse binary, as in Def.В [2](#Thmtheorem2 "Definition 2. вҖЈ Bundling and Set Intersection вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") andВ [21](#Thmtheorem21 "Definition 21. вҖЈ 2.5 Sparse Binary Bundling and Bloom Filter Analysis вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures").

##### Overview of Tools and Techniques

Our analysis of MAP-I establishes the JL property for a variety of random sign matrices, some with dependent entries, that are used to encode bundles, sequences, and bundles of bindings.
In the case of sequences and bindings, the entries of the sign matrices we analyze will not be independent, which complicates our analysis; we get around this using standard concentration results like McDiarmidвҖҷs inequality (TheoremВ [25](#Thmtheorem25 "Theorem 25. вҖЈ 3 Preliminaries and Concentration Inequalities вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures")) and a version for when the bounded differences hold with high probability (CorollaryВ [27](#Thmtheorem27 "Corollary 27. вҖЈ 3 Preliminaries and Concentration Inequalities вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures")).
Our analysis of MAP-B also uses these concentration techniques and also borrows some ideas from Boolean Fourier analysis.
For Hopfield nets and our variation HopfieldВұplus-or-minus\pm, we also use standard concentration results like the Hanson-Wright inequality.
A Bernstein-like variation of McDiarmid, TheoremВ [28](#Thmtheorem28 "Theorem 28 ([ying_mcdiarmids_2004]). вҖЈ 3 Preliminaries and Concentration Inequalities вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"), is key to our analysis of Bloom filters.

#### 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss

##### Bundling and Set Intersection

For MAP-I, we choose Pрқ‘ғP as a scaled sign matrix SВҜВҜрқ‘Ҷ{\bar{S}}.

##### Definition 2.

A *sign vector* yвҲҲ{Вұ1}mрқ‘Ұsuperscriptplus-or-minus1рқ‘ҡy\in\{\pm 1\}^{m} (also called a Rademacher vector) is a vector with independent entries, each chosen uniformly from {Вұ1}plus-or-minus1\{\pm 1\}.
A *sign matrix* SвҲҲ{Вұ1}mГ—dрқ‘Ҷsuperscriptplus-or-minus1рқ‘ҡрқ‘‘S\in\{\pm 1\}^{m\times d} has columns that are independent sign vectors, and a *scaled* sign matrix SВҜ=1mвҖӢSВҜрқ‘Ҷ1рқ‘ҡрқ‘Ҷ{\bar{S}}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{m}}S where Sрқ‘ҶS is sign matrix.

Thus, SвҖӢeiрқ‘Ҷsubscriptрқ‘’рқ‘–Se\_{i} is a random sign vector.
For MAP-I, the bundling operator is addition, so a set Xрқ‘ӢX can be represented as SВҜвҖӢvВҜрқ‘Ҷрқ‘Ј{\bar{S}}v, with v=вҲ‘iвҲҲXeiрқ‘Јsubscriptрқ‘–рқ‘Ӣsubscriptрқ‘’рқ‘–v=\sum\_{i\in X}e\_{i}.
(More typically, MAP-I would use the unscaled sign matrix Sрқ‘ҶS, but SВҜВҜрқ‘Ҷ{\bar{S}} is convenient for analysis and discussion.)
It is known that with high probability, for mрқ‘ҡm sufficiently large, that SВҜВҜрқ‘Ҷ{\bar{S}} satisfies the *Johnson-Lindenstrauss (JL) property*, which is the norm-preserving condition in the lemma below.

##### Lemma 3 ([johnson\_extensions\_1984, achlioptas\_database-friendly\_2003], [JL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johnson-Lindenstrauss_lemma)).

Suppose SВҜвҲҲ1mвҖӢ{вҲ’1,1}mГ—dВҜрқ‘Ҷ1рқ‘ҡsuperscript11рқ‘ҡрқ‘‘{\bar{S}}\in\frac{1}{\sqrt{m}}\{-1,1\}^{m\times d} is a scaled sign matrix (described in Def.В [2](#Thmtheorem2 "Definition 2. вҖЈ Bundling and Set Intersection вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures")).
Then for given Оҙ,Пө>0

рқӣҝitalic-Пө
0\delta,\epsilon>0 there is m=OвҖӢ(ПөвҲ’2вҖӢlogвҒЎ(1/Оҙ))рқ‘ҡрқ‘Ӯsuperscriptitalic-Пө21рқӣҝm=O(\epsilon^{-2}\log(1/\delta)) such that for given vector vвҲҲIвҖӢRdрқ‘ЈsuperscriptIRрқ‘‘v\in\operatorname{{\mathrm{I\!R}}}^{d}, it holds that вҖ–SВҜвҖӢvвҖ–=вҖ–vвҖ–вҖӢ(1ВұПө)normВҜрқ‘Ҷрқ‘Јnormрқ‘Јplus-or-minus1italic-Пө\|{\bar{S}}v\|=\|v\|(1\pm\epsilon), with failure probability at most Оҙрқӣҝ\delta.

This immediately tells us the dimension mрқ‘ҡm required to estimate set sizes up to a multiplicative factor of ОөрқңҖ{\varepsilon}, with failure probability Оҙрқӣҝ\delta.

For X,YвҠҶрқ’і

рқ‘Ӣрқ‘Ң
рқ’іX,Y\subseteq\mathcal{X}, let vрқ‘Јv and wрқ‘Өw denote their characteristic vectors.
An immediate consequence of the JL lemma is that the symmetric difference size |XвҖӢО”вҖӢY|=вҖ–vвҲ’wвҖ–2рқ‘ӢО”рқ‘Ңsuperscriptnormрқ‘Јрқ‘Ө2|X\Delta Y|=\|v-w\|^{2} can be estimated with small relative error as well.

##### Corollary 4.

If random matrix Pрқ‘ғP satisfies the JL property (LemmaВ [3](#Thmtheorem3 "Lemma 3 ([johnson_extensions_1984, achlioptas_database-friendly_2003], JL). вҖЈ Bundling and Set Intersection вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures")),
then for given Оҙ,Пө>0

рқӣҝitalic-Пө
0\delta,\epsilon>0, and a set рқ’ұвҠӮIвҖӢRdрқ’ұsuperscriptIRрқ‘‘\mathcal{V}\subset\operatorname{{\mathrm{I\!R}}}^{d} of cardinality nрқ‘ӣn,
there is m=OвҖӢ(ПөвҲ’2вҖӢlogвҒЎ(n/Оҙ))рқ‘ҡрқ‘Ӯsuperscriptitalic-Пө2рқ‘ӣрқӣҝm=O(\epsilon^{-2}\log(n/\delta)) such that
with failure probability Оҙрқӣҝ\delta, for all pairs v,wвҲҲрқ’ұ

рқ‘Јрқ‘Ө
рқ’ұv,w\in\mathcal{V},
вҖ–PвҖӢ(vвҲ’w)вҖ–2вҲҲвҖ–vвҲ’wвҖ–2вҖӢ(1ВұПө)superscriptnormрқ‘ғрқ‘Јрқ‘Ө2superscriptnormрқ‘Јрқ‘Ө2plus-or-minus1italic-Пө\|P(v-w)\|^{2}\in\|v-w\|^{2}(1\pm\epsilon).

The JL lemma also implies that (PвҖӢv)вҠӨвҖӢ(PвҖӢw)=vвҠӨвҖӢPвҠӨвҖӢPвҖӢwsuperscriptрқ‘ғрқ‘Јtopрқ‘ғрқ‘Өsuperscriptрқ‘Јtopsuperscriptрқ‘ғtopрқ‘ғрқ‘Ө(Pv)^{\top}(Pw)=v^{\top}P^{\top}Pw concentrates around |XвҲ©Y|=vвҠӨвҖӢwрқ‘Ӣрқ‘Ңsuperscriptрқ‘Јtopрқ‘Ө|X\cap Y|=v^{\top}w.

##### Corollary 5.

Suppose the random matrix Pрқ‘ғP satisfies the JL property (LemmaВ [3](#Thmtheorem3 "Lemma 3 ([johnson_extensions_1984, achlioptas_database-friendly_2003], JL). вҖЈ Bundling and Set Intersection вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures")).
Then for v,wвҲҲIвҖӢRd

рқ‘Јрқ‘Ө
superscriptIRрқ‘‘v,w\in\operatorname{{\mathrm{I\!R}}}^{d}, there is m=OвҖӢ(ПөвҲ’2вҖӢlogвҒЎ(1/Оҙ))рқ‘ҡрқ‘Ӯsuperscriptitalic-Пө21рқӣҝm=O(\epsilon^{-2}\log(1/\delta)) so that
vвҠӨвҖӢPвҠӨвҖӢPвҖӢw=vвҠӨвҖӢwВұПөвҖӢвҖ–vвҖ–вҖӢвҖ–wвҖ–superscriptрқ‘Јtopsuperscriptрқ‘ғtopрқ‘ғрқ‘Өplus-or-minussuperscriptрқ‘Јtopрқ‘Өitalic-Пөnormрқ‘Јnormрқ‘Өv^{\top}P^{\top}Pw=v^{\top}w\pm\epsilon\|v\|\|w\|
with failure probabilityВ Оҙрқӣҝ\delta.

Estimation of the cosine of the angle between vрқ‘Јv and wрқ‘Өw, which is |XвҲ©Y|/|X|вӢ…|Y|рқ‘Ӣрқ‘ҢвӢ…рқ‘Ӣрқ‘Ң|X\cap Y|/\sqrt{|X|\cdot|Y|}, up to additive error Пөitalic-Пө\epsilon , is also now immediate.

The goal of our MAP-I bundling section is to use the above lemmas and corollaries to prove the following theorem.

##### Theorem 6.

Suppose random matrix Pрқ‘ғP satisfies the JL property (LemmaВ [3](#Thmtheorem3 "Lemma 3 ([johnson_extensions_1984, achlioptas_database-friendly_2003], JL). вҖЈ Bundling and Set Intersection вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures")).
Given Mрқ‘ҖM pairs of characteristic vectors v,wвҲҲ{0,1}d

рқ‘Јрқ‘Ө
superscript01рқ‘‘v,w\in\{0,1\}^{d} such that for every pair v,w

рқ‘Јрқ‘Өv,w, вҖ–vвҖ–1вҖӢвҖ–wвҖ–1вүӨNsubscriptnormрқ‘Ј1subscriptnormрқ‘Ө1рқ‘Ғ\|v\|\_{1}\|w\|\_{1}\leq N, then there is m=OвҖӢ(NвҖӢlogвҒЎ(M/Оҙ))рқ‘ҡрқ‘Ӯрқ‘Ғрқ‘Җрқӣҝm=O(N\log(M/\delta)) such that вҢҠvвҠӨPвҠӨPwвҢү=vвҠӨw\lfloor v^{\top}P^{\top}Pw\rceil=v^{\top}w for all Mрқ‘ҖM pairs with probability вүҘ1вҲ’Оҙabsent1рқӣҝ\geq 1-\delta.

In short, we inherit much of our capacity analysis of bundling in MAP-I through known results about the JL property.

##### Rotations via JL property.

One operation used in VSAs to expand on the number of nearly orthogonal vectors available for use is via permutations of the entries; this is the вҖңPвҖқ in the MAP VSA systems introduced by [gayler1998multiplicative].
These can be encoded in permutation matrices RвҲҲ{0,1}mГ—mрқ‘…superscript01рқ‘ҡрқ‘ҡR\in\{0,1\}^{m\times m}. We will focus on cyclic permutations.

##### Definition 7.

Let RвҲҲIвҖӢRmГ—mрқ‘…superscriptIRрқ‘ҡрқ‘ҡR\in\operatorname{{\mathrm{I\!R}}}^{m\times m} denote the permutation matrix implementing a rotation, so that Rm,1=1subscriptрқ‘…

рқ‘ҡ11R\_{m,1}=1 and for iвҲҲ[mвҲ’1]рқ‘–delimited-[]рқ‘ҡ1i\in[m-1], Ri,i+1=1subscriptрқ‘…

рқ‘–рқ‘–11R\_{i,i+1}=1, with all other entries equal to zero.

For a random sign vector yрқ‘Ұy, and such a rotation matrix Rрқ‘…R (or indeed for any permutation matrix with few fixed points), RвҖӢyрқ‘…рқ‘ҰRy is nearly orthogonal to yрқ‘Ұy, and the vectors Rв„“вҖӢysuperscriptрқ‘…в„“рқ‘ҰR^{\ell}y for в„“=0,1вҖӢвҖҰвҖӢLв„“

01вҖҰрқҗҝ\ell=0,1\ldots L are pairwise mutually orthogonal with high probability, if LрқҗҝL is not too large.
However, the entries of these vectors are not independent, so additional care is needed in analyzing them.

Permutations (and specifically, rotations) can be used to encode a *sequence* of atomic vectors xв„“superscriptрқ‘Ҙв„“x^{\ell} as a sum вҲ‘в„“Rв„“вҖӢxв„“subscriptв„“superscriptрқ‘…в„“superscriptрқ‘Ҙв„“\sum\_{\ell}R^{\ell}x^{\ell}.
We can also encode a *sequence of sets* with characteristic vectors v(в„“)subscriptрқ‘Јв„“v\_{(\ell)}.

##### Definition 8.

For RвҲҲв„қmГ—mрқ‘…superscriptв„қрқ‘ҡрқ‘ҡR\in{\mathbb{R}}^{m\times m}, SвҲҲIвҖӢRmГ—dрқ‘ҶsuperscriptIRрқ‘ҡрқ‘‘S\in\operatorname{{\mathrm{I\!R}}}^{m\times d} and integer LвүҘ0рқҗҝ0L\geq 0, let SR,LвҲҲв„қmГ—LвҖӢdsubscriptрқ‘Ҷ

рқ‘…рқҗҝsuperscriptв„қрқ‘ҡрқҗҝрқ‘‘S\_{R,L}\in{\mathbb{R}}^{m\times Ld} denote

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | [SвҖӢRвҖӢSвҖӢR2вҖӢSвҖӢвҖҰвҖӢRLвҲ’1вҖӢS].delimited-[]рқ‘Ҷрқ‘…рқ‘Ҷsuperscriptрқ‘…2рқ‘ҶвҖҰsuperscriptрқ‘…рқҗҝ1рқ‘Ҷ[S\;RS\;R^{2}S\;\ldots\;R^{L-1}S]. |  |

For a sequence of v(0),v(1),вҖҰвҖӢv(LвҲ’1)вҲҲв„қd

subscriptрқ‘Ј0subscriptрқ‘Ј1вҖҰsubscriptрқ‘Јрқҗҝ1
superscriptв„қрқ‘‘v\_{(0)},v\_{(1)},\ldots v\_{(L-1)}\in\mathbb{R}^{d}, let vвҲҲв„қLвҖӢdрқ‘Јsuperscriptв„қрқҗҝрқ‘‘v\in\mathbb{R}^{Ld} denote vвүЎ[v(0)вҖӢv(1)вҖӢвҖҰвҖӢv(LвҲ’1)]рқ‘Јdelimited-[]subscriptрқ‘Ј0subscriptрқ‘Ј1вҖҰsubscriptрқ‘Јрқҗҝ1v\equiv[v\_{(0)}\;v\_{(1)}\;\ldots\;v\_{(L-1)}].

The sequence given by vрқ‘Јv in the definition can be represented in MAP-I as a single vector SВҜR,LвҖӢvsubscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷ

рқ‘…рқҗҝрқ‘Ј{\bar{S}}\_{R,L}v.
We first find mрқ‘ҡm such that SВҜR,LsubscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷ

рқ‘…рқҗҝ{\bar{S}}\_{R,L} satisfies the JL property for general vвҲҲв„қLвҖӢdрқ‘Јsuperscriptв„қрқҗҝрқ‘‘v\in\mathbb{R}^{Ld}.

##### Theorem 9.

Given scaled sign matrix SВҜвҲҲIвҖӢRmГ—dВҜрқ‘ҶsuperscriptIRрқ‘ҡрқ‘‘{\bar{S}}\in\operatorname{{\mathrm{I\!R}}}^{m\times d}, rotation matrix RвҲҲIвҖӢRmГ—mрқ‘…superscriptIRрқ‘ҡрқ‘ҡR\in\operatorname{{\mathrm{I\!R}}}^{m\times m} as in Def.В [7](#Thmtheorem7 "Definition 7. вҖЈ Rotations via JL property. вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"), integer L>0рқҗҝ0L>0, and SВҜR,LsubscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷ

Then for vвҲҲIвҖӢRLвҖӢdрқ‘ЈsuperscriptIRрқҗҝрқ‘‘v\in\operatorname{{\mathrm{I\!R}}}^{Ld} as defined above,

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | |вҖ–SВҜR,LвҖӢvвҖ–2вҲ’вҖ–vвҖ–2|вүӨ3вҖӢПөвҖӢвҖ–vвҖ–L,12вүӨ3вҖӢLвҖӢПөвҖӢвҖ–vвҖ–2,superscriptnormsubscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷ  рқ‘…рқҗҝрқ‘Ј2superscriptnormрқ‘Ј23italic-Пөsuperscriptsubscriptnormрқ‘Ј  рқҗҝ123рқҗҝitalic-Пөsuperscriptnormрқ‘Ј2|\|{\bar{S}}\_{R,L}v\|^{2}-\|v\|^{2}|\leq 3\epsilon\|v\|\_{L,1}^{2}\leq 3L\epsilon\|v\|^{2}, |  |

with failure probability 6вҖӢL2вҖӢОҙ6superscriptрқҗҝ2рқӣҝ6L^{2}\delta.

The proof of Theorem [9](#Thmtheorem9 "Theorem 9. вҖЈ Rotations via JL property. вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") relies on partitioning the rows of SВҜВҜрқ‘Ҷ{\bar{S}} so that within the rows of a single partition subset, the corresponding rows of SВҜВҜрқ‘Ҷ{\bar{S}} and RiвҖӢSВҜsuperscriptрқ‘…рқ‘–ВҜрқ‘ҶR^{i}{\bar{S}} can be treated independently.

We get tighter bound on mрқ‘ҡm when the v(i)subscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–v\_{(i)} are characteristic vectors: our bound on mрқ‘ҡm depends on KрқҗҫK, the maximum number of times that a given symbol appears inВ vрқ‘Јv.

##### Theorem 10.

Given scaled sign matrix SВҜвҲҲIвҖӢRmГ—dВҜрқ‘ҶsuperscriptIRрқ‘ҡрқ‘‘{\bar{S}}\in\operatorname{{\mathrm{I\!R}}}^{m\times d}, rotation matrix RвҲҲIвҖӢRmГ—mрқ‘…superscriptIRрқ‘ҡрқ‘ҡR\in\operatorname{{\mathrm{I\!R}}}^{m\times m} (Def.В [7](#Thmtheorem7 "Definition 7. вҖЈ Rotations via JL property. вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures")), integer L>0рқҗҝ0L>0, and SВҜR,LsubscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷ

рқ‘…рқҗҝ{\bar{S}}\_{R,L} as in Def.В [8](#Thmtheorem8 "Definition 8. вҖЈ Rotations via JL property. вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures").
For a sequence of vectors v(0),v(1),вҖҰвҖӢv(LвҲ’1)вҲҲ{0,1}d

subscriptрқ‘Ј0subscriptрқ‘Ј1вҖҰsubscriptрқ‘Јрқҗҝ1
superscript01рқ‘‘v\_{(0)},v\_{(1)},\ldots v\_{(L-1)}\in\{0,1\}^{d}, let
KвүЎвҖ–вҲ‘0вүӨj<Lv(j)вҖ–вҲһрқҗҫsubscriptnormsubscript0рқ‘—рқҗҝsubscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘—K\equiv\|\sum\_{0\leq j<L}v\_{(j)}\|\_{\infty}.
There is m=OвҖӢ(K2вҖӢОөвҲ’2вҖӢlogвҒЎ(K/(ОөвҖӢОҙ)))рқ‘ҡрқ‘Ӯsuperscriptрқҗҫ2superscriptрқңҖ2рқҗҫрқңҖрқӣҝm=O\left(K^{2}{\varepsilon}^{-2}\log(K/({\varepsilon}\delta))\right) such that with failure probabilityВ Оҙрқӣҝ\delta,

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | |вҖ–SВҜR,LвҖӢvвҖ–2вҲ’вҖ–vвҖ–2|вүӨПөвҖӢвҖ–vвҖ–2superscriptnormsubscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷ  рқ‘…рқҗҝрқ‘Ј2superscriptnormрқ‘Ј2italic-Пөsuperscriptnormрқ‘Ј2|\|{\bar{S}}\_{R,L}v\|^{2}-\|v\|^{2}|\leq\epsilon\|v\|^{2} |  |

We handle dependences between rows of Sрқ‘ҶS using a version of McDiarmidвҖҷs inequality (Corollary [27](#Thmtheorem27 "Corollary 27. вҖЈ 3 Preliminaries and Concentration Inequalities вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures")).
As noted by Corollary [4](#Thmtheorem4 "Corollary 4. вҖЈ Bundling and Set Intersection вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") and Corollary [5](#Thmtheorem5 "Corollary 5. вҖЈ Bundling and Set Intersection вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"), satisfying the JL property allows us to find mрқ‘ҡm so we can perform set intersection (dot product) and symmetric difference (subtraction) operations on vectors of form [v(0)вҖӢv(1)вҖӢвҖҰвҖӢv(LвҲ’1)]delimited-[]subscriptрқ‘Ј0subscriptрқ‘Ј1вҖҰsubscriptрқ‘Јрқҗҝ1[v\_{(0)}\,v\_{(1)}\ldots v\_{(L-1)}] up to a multiplicative factor of ОөрқңҖ{\varepsilon} and failure probability Оҙрқӣҝ\delta.

##### Bundles of bindings the JL property.

In MAP-I, we implement binding using the Hadamard (element-wise) products of atomic vectors.
In this setting, we can compactly represent a bundling of kрқ‘ҳk-wise atomic bindings using the matrix SВҜвҠҷksuperscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷdirect-productabsentрқ‘ҳ{\bar{S}}^{\odot k}.

##### Definition 11.

For sign matrix Sрқ‘ҶS, let SвҠҷkвҲҲ1mвҖӢIвҖӢRmГ—(dk)superscriptрқ‘Ҷdirect-productabsentрқ‘ҳ1рқ‘ҡsuperscriptIRрқ‘ҡbinomialрқ‘‘рқ‘ҳS^{\odot k}\in\frac{1}{\sqrt{m}}\operatorname{{\mathrm{I\!R}}}^{m\times\binom{d}{k}}, where each column of SвҠҷksuperscriptрқ‘Ҷdirect-productabsentрқ‘ҳS^{\odot k} is the Hadamard (element-wise) product of kрқ‘ҳk different columns of Sрқ‘ҶS. The scaled version SВҜвҠҷksuperscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷdirect-productabsentрқ‘ҳ{\bar{S}}^{\odot k} is 1mвҖӢSвҠҷk1рқ‘ҡsuperscriptрқ‘Ҷdirect-productabsentрқ‘ҳ\frac{1}{\sqrt{m}}S^{\odot k}. We clarify that PвҠҷkвҠӨsuperscriptрқ‘ғdirect-productabsentlimit-fromрқ‘ҳtopP^{\odot k\top} denotes (PвҠҷk)вҠӨsuperscriptsuperscriptрқ‘ғdirect-productabsentрқ‘ҳtop(P^{\odot k})^{\top}.

With this notation, a bundling of kрқ‘ҳk-wise atomic bindings is SВҜвҠҷkвҖӢvsuperscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷdirect-productabsentрқ‘ҳрқ‘Ј{\bar{S}}^{\odot k}v, for vвҲҲ{0,1}(dk)рқ‘Јsuperscript01binomialрқ‘‘рқ‘ҳv\in\{0,1\}^{\binom{d}{k}}.
Note that
рқ”јвҖӢ[SВҜвҠҷkвҖӢSВҜвҠҷkвҠӨ]=(dk)mвҖӢImрқ”јdelimited-[]superscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷdirect-productabsentрқ‘ҳsuperscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷdirect-productabsentlimit-fromрқ‘ҳtopbinomialрқ‘‘рқ‘ҳрқ‘ҡsubscriptрқҗјрқ‘ҡ{\mathbb{E}}[{\bar{S}}^{\odot k}{\bar{S}}^{\odot k\top}]=\frac{\binom{d}{k}}{m}I\_{m}, while рқ”јвҖӢ[SВҜвҠҷkвҠӨвҖӢSВҜвҠҷk]=I(dk)рқ”јdelimited-[]superscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷdirect-productabsentlimit-fromрқ‘ҳtopsuperscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷdirect-productabsentрқ‘ҳsubscriptрқҗјbinomialрқ‘‘рқ‘ҳ{\mathbb{E}}[{\bar{S}}^{\odot k\top}{\bar{S}}^{\odot k}]=I\_{\binom{d}{k}}.
In order to reason about intersections over bundles of kрқ‘ҳk-bindings, or about the symmetric difference between the bundles of kрқ‘ҳk-bindings, we again establish the JL property, this time for SВҜвҠҷkвҖӢvsuperscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷdirect-productabsentрқ‘ҳрқ‘Ј{\bar{S}}^{\odot k}v.
We first present the result for the k=2рқ‘ҳ2k=2 case, which captures bundles of key-value bindings.

##### Theorem 12.

For vвҲҲ{0,1}(d2)рқ‘Јsuperscript01binomialрқ‘‘2v\in\{0,1\}^{\binom{d}{2}}, there is m=OвҖӢ(ОөвҲ’2вҖӢlog3вҒЎ(вҖ–vвҖ–1/ОөвҖӢОҙ))рқ‘ҡрқ‘ӮsuperscriptрқңҖ2superscript3subscriptnormрқ‘Ј1рқңҖрқӣҝm=O({\varepsilon}^{-2}\log^{3}(\|v\|\_{1}/{\varepsilon}\delta)) so that
for SВҜвҠҷ2вҲҲ{Вұ1m}(d2)superscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷdirect-productabsent2superscriptplus-or-minus1рқ‘ҡbinomialрқ‘‘2{\bar{S}}^{\odot 2}\in\{\pm\frac{1}{\sqrt{m}}\}^{\binom{d}{2}},

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | PrвҒЎ[|вҖ–SВҜвҠҷ2вҖӢvвҖ–2вҲ’вҖ–vвҖ–2|>ОөвҖӢвҖ–vвҖ–2]вүӨОҙ.PrsuperscriptnormsuperscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷdirect-productabsent2рқ‘Ј2superscriptnormрқ‘Ј2рқңҖsuperscriptnormрқ‘Ј2рқӣҝ\Pr[|\|{\bar{S}}^{\odot 2}v\|^{2}-\|v\|^{2}|>{\varepsilon}\|v\|^{2}]\leq\delta. |  |

We have a generalized result for all kрқ‘ҳk as well.

##### Corollary 13.

For scaled sign SВҜвҠҷkвҲҲ{Вұ1m}(dk)superscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷdirect-productabsentрқ‘ҳsuperscriptplus-or-minus1рқ‘ҡbinomialрқ‘‘рқ‘ҳ{\bar{S}}^{\odot k}\in\{\pm\frac{1}{\sqrt{m}}\}^{\binom{d}{k}}, vвҲҲ{0,1}(dk)рқ‘Јsuperscript01binomialрқ‘‘рқ‘ҳv\in\{0,1\}^{\binom{d}{k}}, and iвҲҲ[m]рқ‘–delimited-[]рқ‘ҡi\in[m],
there is C>0рқҗ¶0C>0 and m=OвҖӢ(ОөвҲ’2вҖӢCkвҖӢlogвҒЎkвҖӢlogk+1вҒЎ(kвҖӢвҖ–vвҖ–1/(ОөвҖӢОҙ)))рқ‘ҡрқ‘ӮsuperscriptрқңҖ2superscriptрқҗ¶рқ‘ҳрқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқ‘ҳ1рқ‘ҳsubscriptnormрқ‘Ј1рқңҖрқӣҝm=O(\varepsilon^{-2}C^{k\log k}\log^{k+1}(k\|v\|\_{1}/(\varepsilon\delta))) such that

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | PrвҒЎ[|вҖ–SВҜвҠҷkвҖӢvвҖ–2вҲ’вҖ–vвҖ–2|>ОөвҖӢвҖ–vвҖ–2]вүӨОҙ.PrsuperscriptnormsuperscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷdirect-productabsentрқ‘ҳрқ‘Ј2superscriptnormрқ‘Ј2рқңҖsuperscriptnormрқ‘Ј2рқӣҝ\Pr[|\|{\bar{S}}^{\odot k}v\|^{2}-\|v\|^{2}|>{\varepsilon}\|v\|^{2}]\leq\delta. |  |

The key challenge of establishing the JL property for bundles of bindings is the fact that the columns of SВҜвҠҷksuperscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷdirect-productabsentрқ‘ҳ{\bar{S}}^{\odot k} are not independent; for instance, when k=2рқ‘ҳ2k=2, the columns corresponding to iвҠ—jtensor-productрқ‘–рқ‘—i\otimes j, jвҠ—ktensor-productрқ‘—рқ‘ҳj\otimes k, and iвҠ—ktensor-productрқ‘–рқ‘ҳi\otimes k are dependent.
To track these dependencies, we can represent SВҜвҠҷkвҖӢvsuperscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷdirect-productabsentрқ‘ҳрқ‘Ј{\bar{S}}^{\odot k}v as a hypergraph when vвҲҲ{0,1}(dk)рқ‘Јsuperscript01binomialрқ‘‘рқ‘ҳv\in\{0,1\}^{\binom{d}{k}}.
Then, if we apply McDiarmidвҖҷs inequality to the bundling of bindings, we can obtain the constants used in the bounded differences in terms of the degrees in the hypergraph.

##### Roadmap for Proofs

In В§[4.1](#S4.SS1 "4.1 Bundling and Set Intersection вҖЈ 4 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"), we prove Theorem [6](#Thmtheorem6 "Theorem 6. вҖЈ Bundling and Set Intersection вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") and discuss how the JL frame extends to the sparse JL and Subsampled Randomized Hadamard Transforms (SRHTs).
In В§[4.2](#S4.SS2 "4.2 Rotations for Encoding Sequences вҖЈ 4 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"), we prove Theorems [9](#Thmtheorem9 "Theorem 9. вҖЈ Rotations via JL property. вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") and [10](#Thmtheorem10 "Theorem 10. вҖЈ Rotations via JL property. вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures").
Finally, in В§[4.3](#S4.SS3 "4.3 Binding вҖЈ 4 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"), we prove Theorem [12](#Thmtheorem12 "Theorem 12. вҖЈ Bundles of bindings the JL property. вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") and Corollary [13](#Thmtheorem13 "Corollary 13. вҖЈ Bundles of bindings the JL property. вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures").

#### 2.3 Hopfield Nets and HopfieldВұplus-or-minus\pm

In the early seventies, a simple model of associative memory, based on autocorrelation, was introduced in [nakano\_associatron-model\_1972, kohonen\_correlation\_1972, anderson\_simple\_1972].
In a paper that might be regarded as ushering in the вҖңsecond age of neural networks,вҖқ [hopfield\_neural\_1982] reformulated that model, and described a dynamic process for memory retrieval.

We analyze the *capacity* of HopfieldвҖҷs model, where a collection of vectors constituting the memories is stored.
(A survey of autoasssociative memories is given in [gritsenko\_neural\_2017].)
The capacity problem is to determine the maximum number of such vectors a network can effectively represent in a model described below, and it is assumed that the vectors to be stored are sign vectors.
In our setting, the memories are simply columns of a sign matrixВ SвҲҲ{Вұ1}mГ—nрқ‘Ҷsuperscriptplus-or-minus1рқ‘ҡрқ‘ӣS\in\{\pm 1\}^{m\times n}.

Much of our description of the model paraphrases that of [nakano\_associatron-model\_1972, kohonen\_correlation\_1972, anderson\_simple\_1972].
The neural network in HopfieldвҖҷs model comprises a recurrent collection of neurons with pairwise synaptic connections, with an associated weight matrix WвҲҲв„қmГ—mрқ‘Ҡsuperscriptв„қрқ‘ҡрқ‘ҡW\in{\mathbb{R}}^{m\times m}, such that given input xвҲҲ{Вұ1}mрқ‘Ҙsuperscriptplus-or-minus1рқ‘ҡx\in\{\pm 1\}^{m}, a dynamic process ensues with vectors xвҖӢ[в„“]рқ‘Ҙdelimited-[]в„“x[\ell], where xвҖӢ[0]=xрқ‘Ҙdelimited-[]0рқ‘Ҙx[0]=x, and xвҖӢ[в„“+1]=signвүҘвҒЎ(WвҖӢxвҖӢ[в„“])рқ‘Ҙdelimited-[]в„“1subscriptsignрқ‘Ҡрқ‘Ҙdelimited-[]в„“x[\ell+1]=\operatorname{{\text{sign}\_{\geq}}}(Wx[\ell]).
Here, signвүҘвҒЎ(z)=1subscriptsignрқ‘§1\operatorname{{\text{sign}\_{\geq}}}(z)=1 if zвүҘ0рқ‘§0z\geq 0, and вҲ’11-1 otherwise.
When we reach a fixed point, i.e. xвҖӢ[в„“+1]=xвҖӢ[в„“]рқ‘Ҙdelimited-[]в„“1рқ‘Ҙdelimited-[]в„“x[\ell+1]=x[\ell], the process stops, and xвҖӢ[в„“]рқ‘Ҙdelimited-[]в„“x[\ell] is output.
If a vector xрқ‘Ҙx is a fixed point of the network, the network is said to вҖңrepresentвҖқВ xрқ‘Ҙx.
Typically, the goal is to not only show the fixed-point property for some xрқ‘Ҙx, but also show that for yвҲҲ{0,Вұ1}mрқ‘Ұsuperscript0plus-or-minus1рқ‘ҡy\in\{0,\pm 1\}^{m} close to xрқ‘Ҙx (i.e. yвҠӨвҖӢxsuperscriptрқ‘Ұtopрқ‘Ҙy^{\top}x is large), the network output isВ xрқ‘Ҙx given inputВ yрқ‘Ұy, with high probability.
The capacity problem is to determine how many vectors are represented by a network, as a function of mрқ‘ҡm and a given lower bound on yвҠӨвҖӢxsuperscriptрқ‘Ұtopрқ‘Ҙy^{\top}x.

The weight matrix Wрқ‘ҠW in a Hopfield network is SвҖӢSвҠӨвҲ’nвҖӢImрқ‘Ҷsuperscriptрқ‘Ҷtopрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗјрқ‘ҡSS^{\top}-nI\_{m}, the sum of the outer products of the input vectors with themselves, with the diagonal set to zero.
One motivation for this setup is that such a weight matrix can be learned by an appropriately connected neural network via a Hebbian learning process.

In TheoremВ [14](#Thmtheorem14 "Theorem 14. вҖЈ 2.3 Hopfield Nets and HopfieldВұ вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") below, we give a bound on mрқ‘ҡm and yвҠӨвҖӢSвҲ—jsuperscriptрқ‘Ұtopsubscriptрқ‘Ҷabsentрқ‘—y^{\top}S\_{\*j} so that signвүҘвҒЎ((SвҖӢSвҠӨвҲ’nвҖӢI)вҖӢy)=SвҲ—jsubscriptsignрқ‘Ҷsuperscriptрқ‘Ҷtopрқ‘ӣрқҗјрқ‘Ұsubscriptрқ‘Ҷabsentрқ‘—\operatorname{{\text{sign}\_{\geq}}}((SS^{\top}-nI)y)=S\_{\*j} with bounded failure probability.

##### Theorem 14.

Given matrix SвҲҲ{Вұ1}mГ—nрқ‘Ҷsuperscriptplus-or-minus1рқ‘ҡрқ‘ӣS\in\{\pm 1\}^{m\times n} with uniform independent entries, jвҲҲ[n]рқ‘—delimited-[]рқ‘ӣj\in[n], and ОҙвҲҲ(0,1]рқӣҝ01\delta\in(0,1].
If yвҲҲ{0,Вұ1}mрқ‘Ұsuperscript0plus-or-minus1рқ‘ҡy\in\{0,\pm 1\}^{m} with
yвҠӨвҖӢSвҲ—j/вҖ–yвҖ–вүҘ2вҖӢnвҖӢlogвҒЎ(2вҖӢm/Оҙ)superscriptрқ‘Ұtopsubscriptрқ‘Ҷabsentрқ‘—normрқ‘Ұ2рқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҡрқӣҝy^{\top}S\_{\*j}/\|y\|\geq 2\sqrt{n\log(2m/\delta)}, then with failure probability at mostВ Оҙрқӣҝ\delta, signвүҘвҒЎ((SвҖӢSвҠӨвҲ’nвҖӢIm)вҖӢy)=SвҲ—jsubscriptsignрқ‘Ҷsuperscriptрқ‘Ҷtopрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗјрқ‘ҡрқ‘Ұsubscriptрқ‘Ҷabsentрқ‘—\operatorname{{\text{sign}\_{\geq}}}((SS^{\top}-nI\_{m})y)=S\_{\*j}.
Here it is assumed that the coordinates iрқ‘–i at which yiвү SiвҖӢjsubscriptрқ‘Ұрқ‘–subscriptрқ‘Ҷрқ‘–рқ‘—y\_{i}\neq S\_{ij} are chosen beforeВ Sрқ‘ҶS, or without knowledge of it.

The yвҠӨвҖӢSвҲ—j/вҖ–yвҖ–=yвҠӨвҖӢSвҲ—j/вҖ–yвҖ–1superscriptрқ‘Ұtopsubscriptрқ‘Ҷabsentрқ‘—normрқ‘Ұsuperscriptрқ‘Ұtopsubscriptрқ‘Ҷabsentрқ‘—subscriptnormрқ‘Ұ1y^{\top}S\_{\*j}/\|y\|=y^{\top}S\_{\*j}/\sqrt{\|y\|\_{1}} term may seem mysterious.
mвҲ’вҖ–yвҖ–1рқ‘ҡsubscriptnormрқ‘Ұ1m-\|y\|\_{1} is the number of erasures in yрқ‘Ұy, that is, the number of zero coordinates, and mвҲ’|yвҠӨвҖӢSвҲ—j|рқ‘ҡsuperscriptрқ‘Ұtopsubscriptрқ‘Ҷabsentрқ‘—m-|y^{\top}S\_{\*j}| is the number of erasures plus twice the number of error coordinates iрқ‘–i where yiвү SiвҖӢjsubscriptрқ‘Ұрқ‘–subscriptрқ‘Ҷрқ‘–рқ‘—y\_{i}\neq S\_{ij}.
When there are only erasures, and y=SвҲ—jрқ‘Ұsubscriptрқ‘Ҷabsentрқ‘—y=S\_{\*j} except for errors, вҖ–yвҖ–1=yвҠӨвҖӢSвҲ—jsubscriptnormрқ‘Ұ1superscriptрқ‘Ұtopsubscriptрқ‘Ҷabsentрқ‘—\|y\|\_{1}=y^{\top}S\_{\*j}, and вҖ–yвҖ–1вүҘ2вҖӢnвҖӢlogвҒЎ(2вҖӢm/Оҙ)subscriptnormрқ‘Ұ12рқ‘ӣ2рқ‘ҡрқӣҝ\|y\|\_{1}\geq 2n\log(2m/\delta) suffices.

In В§[5.1](#S5.SS1 "5.1 Analysis of Hopfield Networks via Concentration Bounds вҖЈ 5 Autocorrelation Associative Memories as Bundles of Robust Bindings вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"), we discuss the implications of this result for mрқ‘ҡm in various cases.
If the coordinates of SвҲ—jsubscriptрқ‘Ҷabsentрқ‘—S\_{\*j} are split into two blocks, one block can be retrieved given the other.
This is an alternative sometimes proposed for VSA cleanup, which otherwise involves multiple membership tests.
We also note in the section that the data of a MAP-I bundle of bindings is contained in the Hopfield network, and that robustness under erasures can be used to reduce the size of net.

We also introduce a variant of Hopfield nets, which we call HopfieldВұplus-or-minus\pm, in which the vector outer products yielding Wрқ‘ҠW are each multiplied by a random Вұ1plus-or-minus1\pm 1value before summing.111The name HopfieldВұplus-or-minus\pmВ references the Rademacher values, and is in homage to the many variants of X called X++.
As described in TheoremВ [15](#Thmtheorem15 "Theorem 15. вҖЈ 2.3 Hopfield Nets and HopfieldВұ вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") below, which establishes a JL-like property for HopfieldВұplus-or-minus\pm, this system can store and recover m2superscriptрқ‘ҡ2m^{2} (up to log factors) vectors.
Considering that it uses OвҖӢ(m2)рқ‘Ӯsuperscriptрқ‘ҡ2O(m^{2}) space, its storage efficiency for bundling is not far from that of MAP-I.

##### Theorem 15.

Given Оө,ОҙвҲҲ(0,1]

рқңҖрқӣҝ
01{\varepsilon},\delta\in(0,1], scaled sign matrix SВҜвҲҲ1mвҖӢ{Вұ1}mГ—dВҜрқ‘Ҷ1рқ‘ҡsuperscriptplus-or-minus1рқ‘ҡрқ‘‘{\bar{S}}\in\frac{1}{\sqrt{m}}\{\pm 1\}^{m\times d} with uniform independent entries, diagonal matrix VвҲҲв„қdГ—dрқ‘үsuperscriptв„қрқ‘‘рқ‘‘V\in{\mathbb{R}}^{d\times d}, and diagonal matrix DвҲҲ{0,Вұ1}dГ—dрқҗ·superscript0plus-or-minus1рқ‘‘рқ‘‘D\in\{0,\pm 1\}^{d\times d} with uniform independent Вұ1plus-or-minus1\pm 1 diagonal entries.
There is m=O(ОөвҲ’1log(d/Оҙ)2)m=O({\varepsilon}^{-1}\log(d/\delta)^{2}) such that with failure probability Оҙрқӣҝ\delta,
вҖ–SВҜвҖӢVвҖӢDвҖӢSВҜвҠӨвҖ–F2=(1ВұОө)вҖӢвҖ–VвҖ–F2superscriptsubscriptnormВҜрқ‘Ҷрқ‘үрқҗ·superscriptВҜрқ‘Ҷtopрқҗ№2plus-or-minus1рқңҖsuperscriptsubscriptnormрқ‘үрқҗ№2\|{\bar{S}}VD{\bar{S}}^{\top}\|\_{F}^{2}=(1\pm{\varepsilon})\|V\|\_{F}^{2}.

##### Roadmap for Proofs

Theorem [14](#Thmtheorem14 "Theorem 14. вҖЈ 2.3 Hopfield Nets and HopfieldВұ вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") is proven in В§[5.1](#S5.SS1 "5.1 Analysis of Hopfield Networks via Concentration Bounds вҖЈ 5 Autocorrelation Associative Memories as Bundles of Robust Bindings вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"). Theorem [15](#Thmtheorem15 "Theorem 15. вҖЈ 2.3 Hopfield Nets and HopfieldВұ вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") is discussed in В§[5.2](#S5.SS2 "5.2 HopfieldВұ: Autocorrelation Associative Memories as VSAs вҖЈ 5 Autocorrelation Associative Memories as Bundles of Robust Bindings вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures").

#### 2.4 Analysis of MAP-B

For MAP-B, we write our VSA atomic vectors as SвҖӢeiрқ‘Ҷsubscriptрқ‘’рқ‘–Se\_{i}, where Sрқ‘ҶS is a random sign matrix (Def.В [2](#Thmtheorem2 "Definition 2. вҖЈ Bundling and Set Intersection вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures")).
However, we require here that even composite (non-atomic) VSA vectors be sign vectors, so a bundle of atomic vectors is represented as signвҒЎ(SвҖӢv)signрқ‘Ҷрқ‘Ј\operatorname{{\text{sign}}}(Sv) for a characteristic vector vрқ‘Јv.

The nonlinearity of bundling makes analysis more difficult.
While we were able to reason about set intersection readily via the JL framework when analyzing MAP-I, our results for MAP-B only hold for testing set membership, which is a specific instance of set intersection.
We are able to show that membership testing, to determine if iвҲҲ[d]рқ‘–delimited-[]рқ‘‘i\in[d] is in suppвҒЎ(v)suppрқ‘Ј\operatorname{{\text{supp}}}(v), as represented by the bundle x=signвҒЎ(SвҖӢv)рқ‘Ҙsignрқ‘Ҷрқ‘Јx=\operatorname{{\text{sign}}}(Sv), can be done by checking if xвҠӨвҖӢSвҲ—iвүҘП„superscriptрқ‘Ҙtopsubscriptрқ‘Ҷabsentрқ‘–рқңҸx^{\top}S\_{\*i}\geq\tau, with threshold П„рқңҸ\tau specified below.

##### Theorem 16.

For vвҲҲ{0,1}dрқ‘Јsuperscript01рқ‘‘v\in\{0,1\}^{d},
let x=signвҒЎ(SвҖӢv)рқ‘Ҙsignрқ‘Ҷрқ‘Јx=\operatorname{{\text{sign}}}(Sv) be the MAP-B bundling of n=вҖ–vвҖ–1рқ‘ӣsubscriptnormрқ‘Ј1n=\|v\|\_{1} atomic vectors.
Then for all iвҲҲ[m]рқ‘–delimited-[]рқ‘ҡi\in[m] and jвҲҲsuppвҒЎ(v)рқ‘—suppрқ‘Јj\in\operatorname{{\text{supp}}}(v), PrвҒЎ[xiвҖӢSiвҖӢj=+1]=1/2+ОҳвҖӢ(1/n)Prsubscriptрқ‘Ҙрқ‘–subscriptрқ‘Ҷрқ‘–рқ‘—112Оҳ1рқ‘ӣ\Pr[x\_{i}S\_{ij}=+1]=1/2+\Theta(1/\sqrt{n}), as nвҶ’вҲһвҶ’рқ‘ӣn\rightarrow\infty, and there is m=OвҖӢ(nвҖӢlogвҒЎ(d/Оҙ))рқ‘ҡрқ‘Ӯрқ‘ӣрқ‘‘рқӣҝm=O(n\log(d/\delta)) such that with failure probability Оҙрқӣҝ\delta,
jвҲҲ[d]рқ‘—delimited-[]рқ‘‘j\in[d] has jвҲҲsuppвҒЎ(v)рқ‘—suppрқ‘Јj\in\operatorname{{\text{supp}}}(v) if and only if xвҠӨвҖӢSвҲ—j=ejвҠӨвҖӢSвҖӢsignвҒЎ(SвҖӢv)superscriptрқ‘Ҙtopsubscriptрқ‘Ҷabsentрқ‘—superscriptsubscriptрқ‘’рқ‘—topрқ‘Ҷsignрқ‘Ҷрқ‘Јx^{\top}S\_{\*j}=e\_{j}^{\top}S\operatorname{{\text{sign}}}(Sv) has xвҠӨвҖӢSвҲ—jвүҘ2вҖӢmвҖӢlogвҒЎ(2вҖӢd/Оҙ)superscriptрқ‘Ҙtopsubscriptрқ‘Ҷabsentрқ‘—2рқ‘ҡ2рқ‘‘рқӣҝx^{\top}S\_{\*j}\geq\sqrt{2m\log(2d/\delta)}.

The proof borrows (simple) ideas from Boolean Fourier analysis, namely the analysis of the majority function.
See [o2014analysis] for a thorough guide on this topic.
In В§[6.1.3](#S6.SS1.SSS3 "6.1.3 Testing for Empty Intersection вҖЈ 6.1 Bundling вҖЈ 6 Analysis of MAP-B вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"), we also provide a simple extension of Theorem [16](#Thmtheorem16 "Theorem 16. вҖЈ 2.4 Analysis of MAP-B вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") to testing for whether the set intersection between two sets Xрқ‘ӢX, Yрқ‘ҢY is empty or not.

We also remark that the bundling operator for MAP-B is *not* associative; while signвҒЎ(SвҖӢv)signрқ‘Ҷрқ‘Ј\operatorname{{\text{sign}}}(Sv) is one way that MAP-B might compute a bundle, in a more general setting, there could be a sequence of bundling operations.
This would result in a tree of bundle operations of some depth greater than one, in contrast to signвҒЎ(SвҖӢv)signрқ‘Ҷрқ‘Ј\operatorname{{\text{sign}}}(Sv), whose tree has depth one.
We prove that the reliability of the bundling operation decays exponentially with the depth.

##### Lemma 17.

Given independent sign vectors x(i)вҲҲ{Вұ1}m,iвҲҲ[r]formulae-sequencesuperscriptрқ‘Ҙрқ‘–superscriptplus-or-minus1рқ‘ҡрқ‘–delimited-[]рқ‘ҹx^{(i)}\in\{\pm 1\}^{m},i\in[r], construct vectorВ xрқ‘Ҙx by setting xвҶҗx(1)вҶҗрқ‘Ҙsuperscriptрқ‘Ҙ1x\leftarrow x^{(1)}, and for j=2,вҖҰ,rрқ‘—

2вҖҰрқ‘ҹj=2,\ldots,r, setting xвҶҗsignвҒЎ(x+x(j))вҶҗрқ‘Ҙsignрқ‘Ҙsuperscriptрқ‘Ҙрқ‘—x\leftarrow\operatorname{{\text{sign}}}(x+x^{(j)}).
Then, for в„“вҲҲ[m]в„“delimited-[]рқ‘ҡ\ell\in[m],

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | PrвҒЎ[xв„“(1)вҖӢxв„“=1]=1/2+1/2rPrsubscriptsuperscriptрқ‘Ҙ1в„“subscriptрқ‘Ҙв„“1121superscript2рқ‘ҹ\Pr[x^{(1)}\_{\ell}x\_{\ell}=1]=1/2+1/2^{r} |  |

As a result, great care must be exercised in defining MAP-B bundles for application use.

##### Rotations and Bundles of Bindings

We analyze rotations in the same setting described in Definition [8](#Thmtheorem8 "Definition 8. вҖЈ Rotations via JL property. вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") and Theorem [9](#Thmtheorem9 "Theorem 9. вҖЈ Rotations via JL property. вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"), and bundles of bindings in the setting of Definition [11](#Thmtheorem11 "Definition 11. вҖЈ Bundles of bindings the JL property. вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") and Theorem [12](#Thmtheorem12 "Theorem 12. вҖЈ Bundles of bindings the JL property. вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures").

Our results for MAP-B rotations and bundles of bindings are more limited than what we are able to prove for MAP-I, again due to the nonlinearities present in the binding operation.
As noted before, we only consider single element membership testing.
For sequences, this means checking if a single element iрқ‘–i is present in the jрқ‘—j-th set in a sequence.

##### Theorem 18.

Given a sign matrix SвҲҲIвҖӢRmГ—dрқ‘ҶsuperscriptIRрқ‘ҡрқ‘‘S\in\operatorname{{\mathrm{I\!R}}}^{m\times d} and rotation matrix RвҲҲIвҖӢRmГ—mрқ‘…superscriptIRрқ‘ҡрқ‘ҡR\in\operatorname{{\mathrm{I\!R}}}^{m\times m}, and integer length LрқҗҝL.

The proof of Theorem [10](#Thmtheorem10 "Theorem 10. вҖЈ Rotations via JL property. вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") relies on the MAP-B membership result (Theorem [16](#Thmtheorem16 "Theorem 16. вҖЈ 2.4 Analysis of MAP-B вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures")) and the same trick of partitioning the rows of SR,Lsubscriptрқ‘Ҷ

We will analyze MAP-B bundles of bindings in the restricted setting of key-value pairs.
We can test whether a single keyвҠ—valuetensor-productkeyvalue\text{key}\otimes\text{value} belongs to such a bundle.

##### Theorem 20.

Let vвҲҲ{0,1}(d2)рқ‘Јsuperscript01binomialрқ‘‘2v\in\{0,1\}^{\binom{d}{2}} be such that x=signвҒЎ(SвҠҷ2вҖӢv)рқ‘Ҙsignsuperscriptрқ‘Ҷdirect-productabsent2рқ‘Јx=\operatorname{{\text{sign}}}(S^{\odot 2}v) is a bundle of key-value pairs, as in Def.В [19](#Thmtheorem19 "Definition 19. вҖЈ Rotations and Bundles of Bindings вҖЈ 2.4 Analysis of MAP-B вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures").

##### Roadmap for Proofs

In В§[6.1](#S6.SS1 "6.1 Bundling вҖЈ 6 Analysis of MAP-B вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"), we prove TheoremВ [16](#Thmtheorem16 "Theorem 16. вҖЈ 2.4 Analysis of MAP-B вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures").
In В§[6.1.2](#S6.SS1.SSS2 "6.1.2 Dependence on Depth вҖЈ 6.1 Bundling вҖЈ 6 Analysis of MAP-B вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"), we prove LemmaВ [17](#Thmtheorem17 "Lemma 17. вҖЈ 2.4 Analysis of MAP-B вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures").
Finally the proofs of Theorems [18](#Thmtheorem18 "Theorem 18. вҖЈ Rotations and Bundles of Bindings вҖЈ 2.4 Analysis of MAP-B вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") and [20](#Thmtheorem20 "Theorem 20. вҖЈ Rotations and Bundles of Bindings вҖЈ 2.4 Analysis of MAP-B вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") can be found in В§[6.2](#S6.SS2 "6.2 Rotations вҖЈ 6 Analysis of MAP-B вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") and В§[6.3](#S6.SS3 "6.3 Binding вҖЈ 6 Analysis of MAP-B вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"), respectively.

#### 2.5 Sparse Binary Bundling and Bloom Filter Analysis

If we use VSA vectors BвҖӢxрқҗөрқ‘ҘBx with BрқҗөB chosen as a sparse binary matrix (defined below), we obtain two new families of VSAs, which we refer to as *Bloom filters* and *Counting Bloom filters*, from their names in the data structures literature.

##### Definition 21.

For given mрқ‘ҡm and kвүӨmрқ‘ҳрқ‘ҡk\leq m, a *kрқ‘ҳk-sparse binary vector* yвҲҲ{0,1}mрқ‘Ұsuperscript01рқ‘ҡy\in\{0,1\}^{m} has вҖ–yвҖ–0вүӨksubscriptnormрқ‘Ұ0рқ‘ҳ\|y\|\_{0}\leq k, chosen by adding kрқ‘ҳk random natural basis vectors eiвҲҲ{0,1}m,subscriptрқ‘’рқ‘–superscript01рқ‘ҡe\_{i}\in\{0,1\}^{m}, with each iрқ‘–i chosen independently and uniformly from [m]delimited-[]рқ‘ҡ[m].
A *kрқ‘ҳk-sparse binary matrix* BвҲҲ{0,1}mГ—dрқҗөsuperscript01рқ‘ҡрқ‘‘B\in\{0,1\}^{m\times d} has columns that are independent sparse binary vectors, and a *scaled* kрқ‘ҳk-sparse binary matrix has the form BВҜ=1kвҖӢBВҜрқҗө1рқ‘ҳрқҗө{\bar{B}}=\frac{1}{k}B, where BрқҗөB is a sparse binary matrix.
These may be called just *sparse*, leaving the kрқ‘ҳk implicit.

The Bloom and Counting Bloom filters slightly generalize BSDC-CDT, described in [schlegel2022comparison].
For more on Bloom filters [bloom\_spacetime\_1970], see e.g. [broder\_network\_2004].
A Bloom filter represents the set suppвҒЎ(v)suppрқ‘Ј\operatorname{{\text{supp}}}(v) for vвҲҲ{0,1}dрқ‘Јsuperscript01рқ‘‘v\in\{0,1\}^{d} as 1вҲ§BвҖӢv1рқҗөрқ‘Ј1\wedge Bv, recalling that 1вҲ§BвҖӢv1рқҗөрқ‘Ј1\wedge Bv denotes the vector xрқ‘Ҙx with xi=minвҒЎ{1,(BвҖӢv)i}subscriptрқ‘Ҙрқ‘–1subscriptрқҗөрқ‘Јрқ‘–x\_{i}=\min\{1,(Bv)\_{i}\}.

We give VSA dimension bounds enabling reliable estimation of set intersections; a rigorous version of such an estimator appears to be novel for Bloom filters.
We define a function hm,kвҖӢ(вӢ…)subscriptв„Һ

рқ‘ҡрқ‘ҳвӢ…h\_{m,k}(\cdot) that maps the expected dot product of the VSA bundles to the dot product of the original vectors.

##### Theorem 22.

Let v,wвҲҲ{0,1}d

рқ‘Јрқ‘Ө
superscript01рқ‘‘v,w\in\{0,1\}^{d} represent sets X,Y

рқ‘Ӣрқ‘ҢX,Y respectively, and define the following counts:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | nвүЎ|XвҲ©Y|=vвӢ…w,nvвүЎ|XвҲ–Y|=вҖ–vвҖ–0вҲ’n,nwвүЎ|YвҲ–X|=вҖ–wвҖ–0вҲ’nformulae-sequenceрқ‘ӣрқ‘Ӣрқ‘ҢвӢ…рқ‘Јрқ‘Өsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ‘Јрқ‘Ӣрқ‘Ңsubscriptnormрқ‘Ј0рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ‘Өрқ‘Ңрқ‘Ӣsubscriptnormрқ‘Ө0рқ‘ӣn\equiv|X\cap Y|=v\cdot w,\;\;\;\;\;\;n\_{v}\equiv|X\setminus Y|=\|v\|\_{0}-n,\;\;\;\;\;\;n\_{w}\equiv|Y\setminus X|=\|w\|\_{0}-n |  |

Let x=1вҲ§BвҖӢvрқ‘Ҙ1рқҗөрқ‘Јx=1\wedge Bv and y=1вҲ§BвҖӢwрқ‘Ұ1рқҗөрқ‘Өy=1\wedge Bw, where BвҲҲ{0,1}mГ—dрқҗөsuperscript01рқ‘ҡрқ‘‘B\in\{0,1\}^{m\times d} is a sparse binary matrix.

Assume WLOG nwвүҘnvsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ‘Өsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ‘Јn\_{w}\geq n\_{v}.
Then for ОҙвҲҲ(0,1)рқӣҝ01\delta\in(0,1) and Оө>0рқңҖ0{\varepsilon}>0, there are k=OвҖӢ(ОөвҲ’1вҖӢlogвҒЎ(1/Оҙ))рқ‘ҳрқ‘ӮsuperscriptрқңҖ11рқӣҝk=O({\varepsilon}^{-1}\log(1/\delta))

рқ‘ҡрқ‘ҳвӢ…рқ‘Ҙрқ‘Ұplus-or-minusрқ‘ӣitalic-Пөh\_{m,k}(x\cdot y)=n\pm\epsilon with failure probability Оҙрқӣҝ\delta. Here, hm,kвҖӢ(z)subscriptв„Һ

рқ‘ҡрқ‘ҳрқ‘§h\_{m,k}(z) (see LemmaВ [42](#Thmtheorem42 "Lemma 42. вҖЈ 7.1 Bloom Filters вҖЈ 7 Sparse Binary Bundling and Bloom Filter Analysis via Concentration вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures")) maps the Bloom filter output 1вҲ§BвҖӢz1рқҗөрқ‘§1\wedge Bz to an estimate of вҖ–zвҖ–0subscriptnormрқ‘§0\|z\|\_{0}.

We remark that hm,kвҖӢ(xвӢ…y)subscriptв„Һ

рқ‘ҡрқ‘ҳвӢ…рқ‘Ҙрқ‘Ұh\_{m,k}(x\cdot y) is not an unbiased estimator of vвӢ…wвӢ…рқ‘Јрқ‘Өv\cdot w; we use a вҖңBernstein versionвҖқ of McDiarmid (Theorem [28](#Thmtheorem28 "Theorem 28 ([ying_mcdiarmids_2004]). вҖЈ 3 Preliminaries and Concentration Inequalities вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures")) to establish concentration of xвӢ…yвӢ…рқ‘Ҙрқ‘Ұx\cdot y first, and conclude the success of the estimator hm,kвҖӢ(xвӢ…y)subscriptв„Һ

рқ‘ҡрқ‘ҳвӢ…рқ‘Ҙрқ‘Ұh\_{m,k}(x\cdot y) from there.
In our analysis, we also divide xвӢ…yвӢ…рқ‘Ҙрқ‘Ұx\cdot y into two parts: the 111s contributed by suppвҒЎ(v)вҲ©suppвҒЎ(w)suppрқ‘Јsuppрқ‘Ө\operatorname{{\text{supp}}}(v)\cap\operatorname{{\text{supp}}}(w) after applying BрқҗөB and the min operation, and the 111s contributed by suppвҒЎ(v)вҖӢО”вҖӢsuppвҒЎ(w)suppрқ‘ЈО”suppрқ‘Ө\operatorname{{\text{supp}}}(v)\Delta\operatorname{{\text{supp}}}(w), which may increment the same index after applyingВ BрқҗөB.

In the *Counting Bloom filter*, the bundle is simply BВҜвҖӢvВҜрқҗөрқ‘Ј{\bar{B}}v.
Here, we want to compute the *generalized* set intersection of two vectors v,w

рқ‘Јрқ‘Өv,w, which refers to the coordinate-wise minimum vвҲ§wрқ‘Јрқ‘Өv\wedge w.
The generalized set intersection size is vвҲ§вӢ…w=вҖ–vвҲ§wвҖ–1fragmentsfragmentsвӢ…рқ‘Јрқ‘Өsubscriptnormрқ‘Јрқ‘Ө1v\mathbin{\ooalign{\hfil$\wedge$\hfil\cr\hfil$\cdot$\hfil\crcr}}w=\|v\wedge w\|\_{1}.
Even though the bundle is a linear map, as was the case with MAP-I, we ultimately analyze a non-linear function for set similarity.

##### Theorem 23.

Let v,wвҲҲв„қвүҘ0d

рқ‘Јрқ‘Ө
superscriptsubscriptв„қabsent0рқ‘‘v,w\in{\mathbb{R}}\_{\geq 0}^{d}. Let KbвүЎвҖ–vвҲ’wвҖ–вҲһвүӨmaxвҒЎ{вҖ–vвҖ–вҲһ,вҖ–wвҖ–вҲһ}subscriptрқҗҫрқ‘Ҹsubscriptnormрқ‘Јрқ‘Өsubscriptnormрқ‘Јsubscriptnormрқ‘ӨK\_{b}\equiv\|v-w\|\_{\infty}\leq\max\{\|v\|\_{\infty},\|w\|\_{\infty}\}, and define:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | nвүЎvвҲ§вӢ…w,nvвүЎвҖ–vвҖ–1вҲ’n,nwвүЎвҖ–wвҖ–1вҲ’n,formulae-sequenceрқ‘ӣfragmentsfragmentsвӢ…рқ‘Јрқ‘Өformulae-sequencesubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ‘Јsubscriptnormрқ‘Ј1рқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ‘Өsubscriptnormрқ‘Ө1рқ‘ӣn\equiv v\mathbin{\ooalign{\hfil$\wedge$\hfil\cr\hfil$\cdot$\hfil\crcr}}w,\;\;\;\;\;\;n\_{v}\equiv\|v\|\_{1}-n,\;\;\;\;\;\;n\_{w}\equiv\|w\|\_{1}-n, |  |

Let x=BвҖӢvрқ‘Ҙрқҗөрқ‘Јx=Bv and y=BвҖӢwрқ‘Ұрқҗөрқ‘Өy=Bw, where BвҲҲ{0,1}mГ—dрқҗөsuperscript01рқ‘ҡрқ‘‘B\in\{0,1\}^{m\times d} is a sparse binary matrix.
Then, for ОҙвҲҲ(0,1)рқӣҝ01\delta\in(0,1) and Оө>0рқңҖ0{\varepsilon}>0, there are
k=OвҖӢ(KbвҖӢОөвҲ’1вҖӢlogвҒЎ(1/Оҙ))рқ‘ҳрқ‘Ӯsubscriptрқҗҫрқ‘ҸsuperscriptрқңҖ11рқӣҝk=O(K\_{b}{\varepsilon}^{-1}\log(1/\delta)) and m=12вҖӢПҖ2вҖӢkвҖӢОөвҲ’1вҖӢnvвҖӢnw=OвҖӢ(KbвҖӢОөвҲ’2вҖӢnvвҖӢnwвҖӢlogвҒЎ(1/Оҙ))рқ‘ҡ12superscriptрқңӢ2рқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқңҖ1subscriptрқ‘ӣрқ‘Јsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ‘Өрқ‘Ӯsubscriptрқҗҫрқ‘ҸsuperscriptрқңҖ2subscriptрқ‘ӣрқ‘Јsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ‘Ө1рқӣҝm=12\pi^{2}k{\varepsilon}^{-1}n\_{v}n\_{w}=O(K\_{b}{\varepsilon}^{-2}n\_{v}n\_{w}\log(1/\delta)) such that

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | 1kвҖӢ(xвҲ§вӢ…y)вҲ’(vвҲ§вӢ…w)вҲҲ[0,Пө)1рқ‘ҳfragmentsfragmentsвӢ…рқ‘Ҙрқ‘ҰfragmentsfragmentsвӢ…рқ‘Јрқ‘Ө0italic-Пө\frac{1}{k}(x\mathbin{\ooalign{\hfil$\wedge$\hfil\cr\hfil$\cdot$\hfil\crcr}}y)-(v\mathbin{\ooalign{\hfil$\wedge$\hfil\cr\hfil$\cdot$\hfil\crcr}}w)\in[0,\epsilon) |  |

with failure probability at mostВ Оҙрқӣҝ\delta.
Since nv+nw=вҖ–vвҲ’wвҖ–1subscriptрқ‘ӣрқ‘Јsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ‘Өsubscriptnormрқ‘Јрқ‘Ө1n\_{v}+n\_{w}=\|v-w\|\_{1}, m=OвҖӢ(KbвҖӢОөвҲ’2вҖӢвҖ–vвҲ’wвҖ–12вҖӢlogвҒЎ(1/Оҙ))рқ‘ҡрқ‘Ӯsubscriptрқҗҫрқ‘ҸsuperscriptрқңҖ2superscriptsubscriptnormрқ‘Јрқ‘Ө121рқӣҝm=O(K\_{b}{\varepsilon}^{-2}\|v-w\|\_{1}^{2}\log(1/\delta)) also suffices (using the AM-GM inequality on nvвҖӢnwsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ‘Јsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ‘Өn\_{v}n\_{w}).
If вҖ–vвҖ–1,вҖ–wвҖ–1

subscriptnormрқ‘Ј1subscriptnormрқ‘Ө1\|v\|\_{1},\|w\|\_{1} are stored, then вҖ–vвҲ’wвҖ–1subscriptnormрқ‘Јрқ‘Ө1\|v-w\|\_{1} can be estimated up to additive ОөрқңҖ{\varepsilon} with the sameВ mрқ‘ҡm.

Our theorem helps analyze weighted sets, represented as v,wвҲҲв„ӨвүҘ0d

рқ‘Јрқ‘Ө
superscriptsubscriptв„Өabsent0рқ‘‘v,w\in\mathbb{Z}\_{\geq 0}^{d}, where в„ӨвүҘ0subscriptв„Өabsent0\mathbb{Z}\_{\geq 0} denotes the nonnegative integers.
This also translates to a bound for estimating the в„“1subscriptв„“1\ell\_{1} distance between vрқ‘Јv and wрқ‘Өw, via вҖ–vвҲ’wвҖ–1=вҖ–vвҖ–1+вҖ–wвҖ–1вҲ’2вҖӢ(vвҲ§вӢ…w)subscriptnormрқ‘Јрқ‘Ө1subscriptnormрқ‘Ј1subscriptnormрқ‘Ө12fragmentsfragmentsвӢ…рқ‘Јрқ‘Ө\|v-w\|\_{1}=\|v\|\_{1}+\|w\|\_{1}-2(v\mathbin{\ooalign{\hfil$\wedge$\hfil\cr\hfil$\cdot$\hfil\crcr}}w).

Similarly to our proof of Theorem [22](#Thmtheorem22 "Theorem 22. вҖЈ 2.5 Sparse Binary Bundling and Bloom Filter Analysis вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"), we split 1kвҖӢ(xвҲ§вӢ…y)1рқ‘ҳfragmentsfragmentsвӢ…рқ‘Ҙрқ‘Ұ\frac{1}{k}(x\mathbin{\ooalign{\hfil$\wedge$\hfil\cr\hfil$\cdot$\hfil\crcr}}y) into a contribution related to vвҲ§вӢ…wfragmentsfragmentsвӢ…рқ‘Јрқ‘Өv\mathbin{\ooalign{\hfil$\wedge$\hfil\cr\hfil$\cdot$\hfil\crcr}}w, which is supp(v)вҲ©supp(w)|\operatorname{{\text{supp}}}(v)\cap\operatorname{{\text{supp}}}(w)| for v,wвҲҲ{0,1}d

рқ‘Јрқ‘Ө
superscript01рқ‘‘v,w\in\{0,1\}^{d}, and a contribution from vвҲ’(vвҲ§w)рқ‘Јрқ‘Јрқ‘Өv-(v\wedge w) and wвҲ’(vвҲ§w)рқ‘Өрқ‘Јрқ‘Өw-(v\wedge w), which are the characteristic vectors of suppвҒЎ(v)вҲ–suppвҒЎ(w)suppрқ‘Јsuppрқ‘Ө\operatorname{{\text{supp}}}(v)\setminus\operatorname{{\text{supp}}}(w) and suppвҒЎ(w)вҲ–suppвҒЎ(v)suppрқ‘Өsuppрқ‘Ј\operatorname{{\text{supp}}}(w)\setminus\operatorname{{\text{supp}}}(v) for v,wвҲҲ{0,1}d

рқ‘Јрқ‘Ө
superscript01рқ‘‘v,w\in\{0,1\}^{d}.
The proof of Theorem [23](#Thmtheorem23 "Theorem 23. вҖЈ 2.5 Sparse Binary Bundling and Bloom Filter Analysis вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures") also relies on the вҖңBernstein versionвҖқ of McDiarmidвҖҷs inequality (TheoremВ [28](#Thmtheorem28 "Theorem 28 ([ying_mcdiarmids_2004]). вҖЈ 3 Preliminaries and Concentration Inequalities вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures")).

##### Roadmap for Proofs

In В§[7.1](#S7.SS1 "7.1 Bloom Filters вҖЈ 7 Sparse Binary Bundling and Bloom Filter Analysis via Concentration вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"), we prove TheoremВ [22](#Thmtheorem22 "Theorem 22. вҖЈ 2.5 Sparse Binary Bundling and Bloom Filter Analysis вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"), and in В§[7.2](#S7.SS2 "7.2 Counting Bloom Filters вҖЈ 7 Sparse Binary Bundling and Bloom Filter Analysis via Concentration вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"), we prove TheoremВ [23](#Thmtheorem23 "Theorem 23. вҖЈ 2.5 Sparse Binary Bundling and Bloom Filter Analysis вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures").

#### 2.6 Summary of Contributions

Almost all of our results are summarized in TableВ [3](#S2.T3 "Table 3 вҖЈ 2.6 Summary of Contributions вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures").

The first block of rows are bounds for norm-preserving *linear* operators, so that relative error ОөрқңҖ{\varepsilon} bound for each in estimating вҖ–vвҖ–normрқ‘Ј\|v\| translates to an error bound for estimating вҖ–uвҲ’vвҖ–normрқ‘ўрқ‘Ј\|u-v\| for many pairs of vectors u,v

рқ‘ўрқ‘Јu,v, as in Cor.В [4](#Thmtheorem4 "Corollary 4. вҖЈ Bundling and Set Intersection вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"); dot products, as in Cor.В [5](#Thmtheorem5 "Corollary 5. вҖЈ Bundling and Set Intersection вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures"); and in computing set intersection sizes under a variety of conditions on the set sizes, Thm.В [6](#Thmtheorem6 "Theorem 6. вҖЈ Bundling and Set Intersection вҖЈ 2.2 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures").
  
First block notation:
operation *S* is estimation of size of a set;
*SS* is size of sequence of sets;
*BB* is size of a Bundle of Bindings (set of bound key-value pairs);
matrices PрқҡӮрқҷ№рқҷ»,PрқҡӮрқҡҒрқҷ·рқҡғ

subscriptрқ‘ғрқҡӮрқҷ№рқҷ»subscriptрқ‘ғрқҡӮрқҡҒрқҷ·рқҡғP\_{\mathtt{SJL}},P\_{\mathtt{SRHT}} are sparse JL matrix and SRHT matrix, as discussed in В§[4.1.1](#S4.SS1.SSS1 "4.1.1 Variations Using Alternative Sketching Matrices вҖЈ 4.1 Bundling and Set Intersection вҖЈ 4 Analysis of MAP-I Using Johnson-Lindenstrauss вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures");
KрқҗҫK the maximum number of times a symbol appears in a sequence;
Vрқ‘үV is a diagonal matrix version of vрқ‘Јv;
Dрқҗ·D is a diagonal sign matrix.
  
The second block are operations with non-linear steps. ОөрқңҖ{\varepsilon} is the *additive* estimation error.
  
Second block notation:
operation *MS* is set membership test;
*MSS* is membership in a sequence of sets;
*MKV* is membership in a bundle of bindings, where the bindings are key-value pairs;
*GSI* is generalized set intersection (estimation of vвҲ§вӢ…w=вҲ‘iminвҒЎ{vi,wi}fragmentsfragmentsвӢ…рқ‘Јрқ‘Өsubscriptрқ‘–subscriptрқ‘Јрқ‘–subscriptрқ‘Өрқ‘–v\mathbin{\ooalign{\hfil$\wedge$\hfil\cr\hfil$\cdot$\hfil\crcr}}w=\sum\_{i}\min\{v\_{i},w\_{i}\});
matrix BрқҗөB is a sparse binary matrix, Def.В [21](#Thmtheorem21 "Definition 21. вҖЈ 2.5 Sparse Binary Bundling and Bloom Filter Analysis вҖЈ 2 Technical Overview and Statements of Results вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures");
П„b=2вҖӢmвҖӢlogвҒЎ(2вҖӢd/Оҙ)subscriptрқңҸрқ‘Ҹ2рқ‘ҡ2рқ‘‘рқӣҝ\tau\_{b}=\sqrt{2m\log(2d/\delta)};
kрқ‘ҳk is the number of nonzeros per column ofВ BрқҗөB;
hm,kвҖӢ(z)=1kвҖӢlog1вҲ’1/mвҒЎ(1вҲ’z/m)subscriptв„Һ

рқ‘ҡрқ‘ҳрқ‘§1рқ‘ҳsubscript11рқ‘ҡ1рқ‘§рқ‘ҡh\_{m,k}(z)=\frac{1}{k}\log\_{1-1/m}(1-z/m), defined in Lem.В [42](#Thmtheorem42 "Lemma 42. вҖЈ 7.1 Bloom Filters вҖЈ 7 Sparse Binary Bundling and Bloom Filter Analysis via Concentration вҖЈ Capacity Analysis of Vector Symbolic Architectures");
v,wвҲҲ{0,1}d
